<Author>hotelreviewer333
<Content>Have to Agree--Watertown is GREAT After trying all different Seattle downtown and north/south metro hotels over the years, I gave Watertown a shot based on all the great reviews and--wow--was everybody right! I was there 4 nights and it poured pretty much everyday but was a restful and relaxing place to stay. I had a suite which reminded more of some of the modern boutique hotels I've stayed in large cities in Australia and Europe. I loved that the windows opened (European style) and the spaciousness of the suite, and all the funky yet very nice decorations. Breakfast bar each morning was better than most any I've ever had--who has guava juice besides here? The free parking was also a draw for me and saved me a good $80 over the downtown hotels that charge an arm  a leg. I had a trade show at the Seattle convention center and it was a snap getting there  back--less than 10 minutes even with Seattle's notoriously horrible traffice on I-5. When it wasn't raining I did get out to walk to the shops  restaurants in the University District, which were just a few minutes away. This hotel is very convenient off of I-5 and in the U District, but was very quiet and located in a nice non-busy neighborhood. I'll never stay anywhere else in Seattle from now on!

<Author>NoCal_BizTraveler
<Content>Pouring Rain - Great Hotel I stayed one night at the Watertown for a meeting at UW. Not sure where to start. The flight was terrible, weather wet, and meeting mediocre. The hotel was perfect.First, I drove into the secure underground parking lot - dry and out of the wind. Perfect.Next, upon checking in I was given a flight of wine at the hotel's lovely lounge. They also had a nice bowl of fresh, hot, organic and local soup with bread. Finished with warmed cookies. And a pick of a very nice local wine for a great price. Perfect.The room was simple with some nice touches. First they gave me the book lovers cart (free) with lots of fun books to read. When I come back with my baby, we'll get the art cart or kids cart (or both!). Coffee, tea and popcorn (unlike chains, they don't charge you $10 to touch the stuff, it's included). Filtered water, nice bathroom and a sink with drawers. Perfect.The rooms were business traveler AND kid friendly. Very bright and airy. Windows opened in a kid-safe manner, room was spacious, and my view was of the UW campus and bay.Lastly, they accommodated me by letting me keep my car in the garage rather than making me go find parking on campus after I checked out. They also gave me a nifty map with my room key. Staff were friendly locals who made sure everything I needed was available to me.I've been staying at Hyatts, W, Omni hotels for a month on travel and this one seemed to be the perfect blend of just what I needed without the fuss (and added expenses) of other hotels.I will absolutely return this summer with my family and next year for my annual meeting at UW.

<Author>Sciencewriter
<Content>Loved this unique hotel The Watertown's tagline is a unique urban hotel and it truly is! I stayed here for a one-night business meeting and then I was taking a red-eye flight to the East Coast the next day. I could not have asked for a better night's sleep and a more relaxing, enjoyable experience. The staff were not just helpful and friendly, they would bend-over-backwards to help you in any way they could. The hotel has very modern furnishings and many tiny extras that add up to a wonderful stay (cookies at check-in, Aveda toiletry products, terry cloth robes, filtered tap water in rooms, coffee/tea/popcorn/microwave, free shuttle around town). The included breakfast was not your standard pastries and fruit and cold cereal, but all that, plus eggs, bacon, toast, bagels, yogurt, hot cereal, etc etc. The absolute best part of this hotel are the free A La Cartes they will bring to your room--I got the spa cart with a foot bath, relaxing CDs and player, aromatherapy, and massagers. It was great and they have lots of other great carts for kids or a rainy day, too. I did not get a chance to use my complimentary wine tasting coupon in the attached wine bar, but I'm sure it would have been as wonderful as everything else associated with the Watertown! If you are headed to the University of Washington campus or just want to stay a bit outside of downtown Seattle, this is the place for you! It's not incredibly cheap (with taxes, my night was about $170), but it's well worth it when you figure in breakfast, a free wine tasting, and excellent customer service!

<Author>AEC in SF
<Content>Our new fave hotel in Seattle We always rent a car, so the location's fabulous for us -- you're so close to I-5 and 45th Street that getting anywhere in town is simple and fast, and free parking in a secure garage can't be beat. If you're doing the usual tourist stuff, they'll drop you off downtown in their shuttle.The design is modern but not too wild; the beds are comfy, and the views gorgeous. The bathroom layout is great for two people: the toilet and shower are in a private room, and there's a large vanity in the dressing area, separated from the sleeping area by a freestanding closet that opens from both sides.Free breakfast is so-so, but you get what you pay for.The people who work here were very helpful and polite; housekeeping stayed out of our hair when we wanted to sleep in, and yet managed to clean the room every day.We paid $145 a night for a room that would have cost close to twice that amount downtown.

<Author>Oswego73
<Content>The Watertown: Great rooms, great views! We live nearby, and when we had to (on very short notice) move out of our house for a week during some remodelling work, we found the Watertown online, and booked a week there. I'd known friends who'd stayed there because it was near the University, but we'd never been there and had just driven by on occasion. Our experience was top-notch: we showed up about an hour after we'd made the reservation online (and about 2 hours after our contractor told us that we'd need to vacate our home for 5 days!), and they were very organized, and prepared, given that we'd just made the reservation. Our room was beautiful, and the view of Lake Union and Queen Anne was lovely. We enjoyed the proximity to the U-District, and ended up walking everywhere or taking the bus downtown... it was easiest just to leave the car in the parking garage and hop on a bus to get downtown, or just walk a couple of blocks to dinner, shopping, and grocery stores. Plus we could walk to all the movie theaters. So, we ended up having an unexpected but great stay in the Watertown, and had a fabulous time exploring the area on foot, which we hadn't done for ages. The fixtures, linens, and finishes were all luxurious and elegant, and our room felt very spacious. The staff made our stay even better: they were professional, welcoming, and helped us with bus schedules and movie times. The breakfast was also decent: we didn't expect The Four Seasons, but it was miles above a typical continental breakfast in a hotel chain. Real coffee, fresh juice, and organic yogurt w/ fresh fruit. Yum!

<Author>Apala
<Content>A great hotel! Our family thoroughly enjoyed our 2-night stay at the Watertown. On first sight, it actually looked more like a new condominium. The room was spacious, modern, clean and well kept. We even had a great view of Mount Rainier, the Space Needle, and parts of downtown Seattle. The staff were very courteous, helpful, and obviously took a lot of pride in their hotel. The breakfast was very good and satisfying. The surf cart (computer and printer) was a real bonus as it allowed me to help plan the rest of our vacation in the Pacific Northwest. The free downtown shuttle was very convenient and a real cost saver, reducing the number of days of renting a car. When we did get a car, the secured underground parking came at no extra charge, unlike most hotels in the downtown area. It is conveniently located in the University area with its wide variety of restaurants, markets, stores, and bus routes. Just about our only disappointment was not having enough time to take advantage of the hotel's free bicycles and explore the nearby trails and not being able to get reservations here during the third portion of our trip. The Watertown is a truly unique hotel and I wish that there were more hotels like it throughout the U.S.

<Author>ESLer
<Content>Excellent hotel This is an excellent alternative to the hotels in the crowded downtown area. The Watertown is in the university district of Seattle. The rooms are large, with great views, spotless and extremely quiet. The staff were uniformly helpful. The breakfast (included in the rate) was superb, and there is a daily wine tasting, free to hotel guests. Bicycles are free so you can bike in the area or to nearby parks (Green Lake is good). Within walking distance are many small restaurants serving different ethnic foods and several good bookstores. The hotel also provides a free shuttle to and from downtown. I can say nothing negative about this hotel!

<Author>iraform
<Content>Very accommodating I expected the Watertown Hotel to be a nice place 鈥?and it was 鈥?but the thing that separated it from the pack of hotels I've stayed at lately is the attitude of the employees. Whatever you asked, it seemed, the answer was Yes. Can I get a computer in my room? Sure. Can I use your office computer to print out 60 sheets of data? No problem. Call me a car that can take me to the airport for a more-than-reasonable price? Right away. There was never any of that infuriating, Sorry, I'll have to ask the manager, or, Corporate says we're not allowed to do that. I asked, and they said yes 鈥?even when I took more than one chocolate chip cookie.A few more nice things about Watertown: The rooms are well laid out, with the bathroom and dressing area tucked away in a private nook behind the TV stand-wardrobe; the University District restaurants, coffee houses, and shops are a five-minute walk away 鈥?closer than it looks on a map 鈥?and downtown Seattle is a 10-minute drive; the free breakfast (eggs, bacon, fruit, bagels, toast, spreads, juices, cereals) is generous, and the restaurant area and outside tables are great spots to relax with a cup of coffee all through the day; the parking is free! Fourteen members of my family stayed at Watertown and its sister property the University Inn, which is a block down the street. The Watertown is definitely an adult hotel. The University Inn is better for children, with more of a family vibe and a nice little pool. I'd stay at either one again.

<Author>Mitch&Ove
<Content>What a find! If you're visiting Seattle and you don't mind being an easy 20 min bus ride away from downtown then book this hotel!!Stayed in the Watertown Hotel after reading good reviews on Tripadvsor. So glad we did! The room was lovely - big, beautifully furnished and equipped (massive bed, airconditioned, great bathroom, microwave- complete with popcorn, starbucks coffee provided etc etc) and the hotel was clean and smart. We turned up for the complimentary breakfast, thinking it would be a curled up danish and lukewarm coffee to find that there was a choice of juices, cereals, bagels, danishes, eggs, bacon, sausages, yoghurts, and loads more). The hotel provided free, secure parking, a laundry, free loan of bikes, a gym and best of all, complimentary carts. Order them when you book or arrive and a cart will be delivered to your room. We borrowed the relaxation cart (lovely spa products - body lotion, bath salts etc, a food spa, massage machine, CD player and relaxing cd's) and the internet cart (computer and printer), but there were loads more on offer - a games cart (lots of board games), kids cart (plug socket covers, kids bath toys etc), grumpy cart (not sure what was on this) night night cart (aromatherapy products and white noise machine) to name a few. Although the hotel is a bus ride out of Seattle's centre, it was still a great location, in the middle of the University district. There were lots of good bars  restaurants just a block away. The hotel provides a free shuttle service downtown and it's also on main bus routes. We reckoned this was one of the best hotels we'd ever stayed in when you considered the location, room, standard of breakfast, service etc. Didn't want to leave  would definately stay there if we ever visit Seattle.

<Author>farlucy
<Content>U-District Find! We just spent a long weekend at the Watertown. We really enjoyed the unique amenities such as complementary bicycles, evening wine-tasting, free shuttle, and chocolate chip cookes. Guests can also request themed 'carts'. We chose the spa cart, which included a foot messager and message wand. The hotel is clean and rooms are generous in size. They gave us a complementary upgrade to a suite, which was great. Large room with living/dining area. Only minor complaints: wireless internet was pretty slow (although we never tried using their cable connection), and once the shuttle left without us despite our having made reservations. Suggest if you plan to use the shuttle be downstairs and on watch for its arrival.

<Author>fluoresce
<Content>great for business travelers, singles and couples I've been traveling to Seattle from the San Francisco Bay Area every week for the past two months (late April-late June 2006) and my favorite hotel I've ever stayed at for any business trip is the Watertown. I look forward to staying there, if it's not already booked up for my trip. It's been pretty busy since the summer started.It feels more like an apartment than a conventional hotel. For me it's a home away from home. It's relatively new so everything in the rooms and the lobby is modern and clean. The parking garage is well-lit. The rooms all have microwaves and mini-fridges. The breakfast (eggs and bacon, yogurt, fruit, yummy scones that are cookie-like, juices), complimentary wine tasting 5pm-9pm, Hershey's chocolates in the rooms are nice touches. There's a minimart type area in the lobby if you need some quick snacks. I've heard good things about the free carts (art, relaxing, computer or movie) too, but haven't done that yet.Unlike some downtown Seattle hotels (Watertown is not in downtown but near University of Washington), parking is free.Potential downsides - checkout, if you want a receipt when you leave, is at the counter only. Shuttle to downtown stops at 7pm and is only hourly, which may not be often enough if you want to sightsee or shop downtown. The neighborhood isn't really touristy as far as walking around for stuff to do. These aren't that important to me, so it depends on what you're looking for.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I really wanted to like the Watertown, but...... Our first two days at the Watertown were great. We enjoyed the complimentary breakfast and the chocolate chip cookies in the lobby. It was a good value for the price we were paying....until our 3rd day.We left at 7am in the morning and when we returned at 3pm I was surprised to see a maid's cart on the floor. I didn't think much of it until we went in our room and saw that the room wasn't made up. We were in town for a wedding that was starting in 2 hours, so we picked up a couple towels from the floor and started getting ready. While I was in the shower housekeeping stopped by. My husband explained that we were getting ready and to come back after 4pm. A few minutes later we got a call from the front desk saying that if we didn't get our room cleaned right then that it wouldn't be cleaned at all. Finally the front desk said that the room would be made up after 6pm. That was fine with us, since we were going to be out until late in the evening. To our surprise at 4pm housekeeping showed up again. We were almost ready, so told them to come back in 10 minutes and we would be gone. Two minutes later the front desk called and said that the maid had left and that our room would not be cleaned up. The conversation went back and forth with the front desk. Even at a Motel 6 I expect to have my room made up. In the end as we were leaving I gave the front desk my blackberry number and told them to have the manager call me if they were unable to get our room cleaned. The clerk at the front desk (who was giving us some serious attitude) got off the phone (with whom appeared to be the offsite manager) and announced that she was going to clean our room and to not exepct much since she wasn't a trained housekeeper.We returned to a room that appeared to be cleaned, except for that there were no bath towels in the room and instead we were left with 5 bath mats! Maybe that was the clerk's way of getting even with us.The front desk appeared to be staffed by college students and not once between Thursday and Sunday did we see a manager or someone who appeared over 25 years old. I really question who is in charge here. I shouldn't have to argue with a clerk over whether my room is going to be cleaned, especially when I was gone for 8 hours during the day. I did contact the manager when I returned home. They did say that my experience should not have happened. They offered me $20 off a future stay. No thank you. I'd rather stay some place where I can be assured of clean towels and no attitude!If everything is going well and you have low expectations, I think the Watertown is a fine place to stay. But if anything out of the ordinary happens (like housecleaning not being able to get rooms clean by 3pm), good luck!!!

<Author>Cousin_Jeff
<Content>Great Location + Lots of Perks My daughter is interested in attending the University of Washington, so she and I visited Seattle in April and stayed at the Watertown. It's only a few blocks from the UW campus - easy walking distance.The hotel had many amenities that appealed to us and made it our choice over the cheaper hotels available in the campus area:- Bikes and helmets are available free of charge. We took a nice ride along the nearby Burke-Gilman Trail. However, their bikes were not in the best condition. They told me some were in the shop, and those that were left were barely adequate. If you're a serious biker, I'd call ahead and make sure there are some good ones available.- Free carts of various entertainments were available. It turned out we didn't use any, but I can see how they'd be great for families with young kids in particular.- Free high-speed Internet.- Free shuttle to the downtown (and back).- Free breakfast, which isn't at Embassy Suites quality, but does include scrambled eggs, cereal, and scones. And there are chocolate chip cookies in the lobby.Rooms are nicely sized and attractive. Also lots of cable channels available. The Starbucks coffee and candies were a nice touch too.There is also a reasonably priced shuttle (Town Car!) service to and from the airport, so we didn't have to rent a car or pay for parking. Info is on their web site.Overall, I'd say it's a very good value for the Seattle area, and I'd recommend the hotel to anyone.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Experience We had a great experience at this hotel. We chose it because it is located close to the University of Washington and we were visiting our son. However it has many other benefits that will make us stay there again. For example, they have free parking, a very nice and convenient buffet breakfast, carts with videos, computers, or other interests which are available without charge, and a washer/dryer on your floor which can be used without charge. They also have wine tasting in the evening. We borrowed their bicycles to get some exercise and visit the Gasworks park. It was a great experience. The staff is very helpful and friendly. It also is a very secure hotel in which you have to use your charge card type key in the elevators to go up to your floor. The only negative thing I can contribute is that they need to maintain their bicycles better. Otherwise I would recommend that Watertown Hotel to anyone visiting Seattle, especially if you wabt to stay near UW.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not quite as advertised This hotel definitely does have some nice elements -- the decor, for example. It's relatively new, clean, and the parking was free and convenient. The free internet access in the room was quick and easy. But overall, it was billed with more hype than it delivered. It pretends to be hip and urban, but it's just a small-town hotel with limited amenities:-- Our city view room with king bed was small, and the bathroom had barely enough room to turn around in. And don't bother paying for that city view. Ours was obstructed by neighboring buildings. -- Breakfast is merely weak Starbucks coffee, some boiled eggs and a lot of sugar and bread. Go down to the Portage Bay Cafe instead and buy a remarkable breakfast.-- The shuttle service that supposedly makes several downtown stops made just one, and the latest pickup back to the hotel is 7:30 p.m. -- The wine tasting had an expansive list -- but it was limited to two tastings (each of which was about three sips). No cheese or bread was offered with the tastings.-- There is no room service, and no food at the restaurant on weekends. The week night menu is very limited. However, the nearby Portage Bay Cafe is excellent! However, it closes at 3 p.m. and there's nothing decent within walking distance. If you want to eat dinner, you'll need to find your own transportation or you'll need to take the shuttle downtown (and remember, you'll need to catch the last shuttle back by 7:30 p.m.)-- There's no pool. If you want to swim, you'll need to walk to a neighboring hotel.-- There's no express check out; no pre-bill under your door on the day of your departure.-- Forget the carts. You get to choose just one, regardless of the length of your stay. We chose the CD cart, which amounted to a boombox left on the bed.  
<Date>Mar 31, 2006

<Author>chauchat
<Content>Try the relaxation package... We just stayed at Watertown last week. If you don't mind being away from downtown, it's a fun place to be. We loved our suite--it was large and open, with built-in furnishings. The staff couldn't be more friendly and helpful--we were out of toothpaste, and the person at the desk went to the sister hotel to get us a tube. The cartes are a lot of fun--ours had all kinds of goodies to help us relax, which was precisely what we were there for. Everything is inexpensive--free breakfast and wine tasting during the week, tasty snacks with the wine which for us served as a light dinner. If you have a choice, and you are going to spend time in the room, I would recommend a suite. The regular rooms are fine, but the spacious feel of the suite is much nicer.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Free Bikes This is a great hotel with lots of nice touches. We stayed in June and had a fabulous time making full use of the free bicycles to travel around Seattle - the pool and the gym are very good too. <Author>ZweiHunde
<Content>Great value My wife and I recently spent a night at the Watertown hotel near theUniversity of Washington campus due in large part to the positive reviews posted on this web site. I must say the reviews were right on. This is a well designed hotel with large rooms(King studio), decent location, nice beds, good service and great added extras(wine tasting, free bike use and underground parking). My wife and I also stayed at the Westin downtown on this trip andthe only advantages the Westin has are location and views. Although theWatertown isn't Downtown Seattle it has easy access to great area restaurants (we enjoyed Serafina). The Watertown has 4* accommodations at 3* prices and is worth the savings if you don't mind driving or taking the free shuttle down town. I would also recommending biking through the UW campus the beauty is worth the hills!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Can't miss with the Watertown! This past August, my family and I had the pleasure to stay at the Watertown Hotel. As advertised, this is indeed a unique hotel. A modern and chic place with comfortable beds and well layed-out rooms. We booked two rooms -- a regular room and a suite. The suite was huge -- and regular room was above average. Furniture in each room was fit for a nice home. Staff was helpful and friendly with no detection of any attitude. The price is moderate to low for the business traveler, perhaps a bit on high end for the family/budget traveler. However, everything is included for one price. Underground well-lit parking, a newspaper, internet access, a great breakfast with Starbucks coffee, the gym, Friday evening wine tasting were all free of charge. The hotel delivered an artist cart to one room and a spa cart to the second at no charge! Each floor has a washer/dryer nicely hidden behind a key-entry closet which came in handy. The hotel is in a residential neighborhood with good restaurants, close to parks and transportation, and 3 blocks from Trader Joes to stock up on snacks and inexpensive wine! For a business traveler who often stays at 4 or 5 star hotels, this hotel is right up there with the best and was indeed a unique experience in a wonderful city!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel, comfortable My friend and I stayed at Watertown August 19-21, based on recommendation of a friend who stayed there before, as well as all the great reviews on TripAdvisor. I thought the beds were comfortable, and I loved the decor - though if more than 2 people had lots of clothing, there were not a lot of drawers. Did not discover popcorn until we left! We had one of the rooms on a higher floor -view was overlooking vacant lot and parking lot, as well as part of Seattle skyline and Mt Rainier.Loved being by University of Washington and strolling up and down University Way. Restaurants and stores within a few minutes walk -like different ethnic restaurants. A couple of drugstores to pick up last minute items before our cruise. We did not have a car, used hotel shuttle bus (make reservation in advance for shuttle). There are also city buses that you can take into downtown (cabs are not cheap).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A very decent hotel The Watertown Hotel is a really decent place to stay in terms of both quality and value. Our large twin room was clean and comfortable, with Aveda bath products and even a discreet microwave complete with popcorn! The contintental breakfast which is included in the price is also good, you can have bagels, cereal, toast, as well as Starbucks coffee and juice. Plus, don't worry about the fact that it's not 'in town', as you can take a bus from right outside (it really doesn't take long, about 15 mins), or book a place on the free shuttle bus service. It's also really close to the arty enclave of Freemont, which has numerous funky resturants and boutiques. In fact, instead of going downtown, we preferred going there or to nearby Wallingford for dinner.And for no extra cost, you can also have the fun of choosing a 'cart' for your room which you can have for the duration of your stay. There's the TV/DVD cart ( which we chose), the internet cart, the pampering cart, the baby cart etc.. etc... You don't have to take it but it's a nice touch.Also, if you're driving, parking in the underground car park is included in the price. Result!

I don't think we'll ever stay there again. It had a very cold feeling to us, even though the staff was very warm, more of a business traveler hotel I think.

<Author>fluffymichou
<Content>pleasant stay in Watertown We stayed at the Watertown hotel after reading all the great reviews. Definitely it is a nice, clean hotel in a safe quiet neighborhood, right by Safeco. All the rooms have a modern, clean style. the hotel itself is quite new, maybe 5-10 years old. the parking is free (which is a plus considering downtown hotels charge for parking). the complimentary breakfast is a very generous buffet consisting of boiled eggs, frozen waffles, selection of teas and starbucks coffee, jam, butter, toast, cereal, oatmeal, yogurt, some fresh fruits. within walking distance, there are plentiful restaurants just one street over, situated right by the university of washington where you can get good cheap eats and soak in the college atmosphere. other amenities that are nice include aveda hair and skin products in the bathrooms, and you can get a complimentary cart. i got the spa cart which had some nice bath products and a foot massager and relaxing cd. the only gripe i had is driving in to downtown seattle for tourist activities may prove a chore as seattle traffic can be a bit bad. i might try a downtown hotel next time i visit seattle, just to get a better feel for the sophistication of this city. overall though, Watertown is a great hotel for the money.

<Author>kawai888
<Content>Great hotel, reasonable price Our family of 4 recently stayed at the Watertown hotel. It is a new hotel and our room (2 queen beds) are tastefully decorated. The bath soaps and lotions came from Aveda, a well know brand. The windows are insulted and you don't hear the noise from the streets. THere isn't much tourist activities close by but good resturants and shops are all within short driving distance. U of Washingon is next door and the hotel will lend you a bike to ride around campus. <Content>Mixed review for Watertown Overall the Watertown property is fresh and original. I appreciated that parking and breakfast are included. Not what I expect for a $200 room.Note: I rate this hotel above average based on the decor, cleanliness and amenties of the room, which are more important to me than service. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our Car Liked it Best Let's be upfront here. The whole point of the Watertown can be summed up by boutique-ish hotel with convenient and free parking. My friends who are sales reps swear by it, so when my work associates and I scheduled a couple of days in Seattle, it seemed like a good choice.The room is newish, looks a bit like an apartment. The windows open. I wasn't crazy about the storage space. The decor is simple. There's a microwave. You can pretend (the way some of my friends do) that you are not on vacation, but actually live in the city you are visiting. OK, so you live in the student ghetto. But there are about a half dozen teriyaki stands to choose from; what more did you want? It's a short drive to better restaurants on Capital Hill.The cart system is clever, but the computer cart is somewhat unworkable. It's hard to comfortbly use. A computer room would work better. My work friends love free hotel breakfasts so let me say it was appreciated by some. For me, eh. Really, it's all about the free parking and easy freeway access. And for tourist stuff, downtown is better.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Definately a unique urban hotel The previous reviewers were right on the overall cleanliness, decor, amenities of the hotel and the low scale ethnic eateries around the neighborhood. I would like to add my comments on the ala cart amenities and the staff. I agree with some reviews that the ala cart does not offer much practical sense. It is somewhat gimmicky. We ordered a movie cart and when it arrived, my husband and I looked at each other and started laughing ( go to their website and see it yourself). It also appeared that there was only one cart for every a la cart item. We couldn't get the spa cart because someone already got it for the night. The staffs are friendly but they also seem extremely busy. The night we checked in, only one front desk personnel was on duty. He was very busy answering MULTIPLE phone calls while checking us him. When we called down for the morning call service, a young guy on the other line was yarning. I believe most staffs are students. In some way we felt like we were staying at a training hotel.For its price, the hotel is of great value but a rental car is a must if you want to do some sightseeing. A morning jog around the campus was a surprising pleasure-- -beautiful architecture, landscape, and gardens. I visited the reading room in the Suzzallo Library and walked through the waterfront trail around the Union Bay. Both were stunning in their own way--one is man-made and the other is natural. Would I stay here next time? Definitely, if I were on a business trip. If I were in Seattle with family for a vacation, I would stay somewhere else because the decor though hippy does not render a sense of warmth and coziness.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This Cool hotel lost me with the Uncomfortable bed Most of the other reviews hit the nail on the head. This hotel is hip and unlike any other you have ever been too. The furnishings are unusual and kind of fun. The cart program is kind of cool, but more gimmicky than practical. The location is not ideal for tourist activities, but a rental car (free parking) can easily solve that. The staff is courteous, but generally are a bit too busy (check-in and check-out were both over 5 minutes). The free continental breakfast is a nice touch, but not of superior quality. The fitness room is VERY small and not private (it opens to the breakfast area and has sidewalk-level windows in a busy college area).Unfortunately, a comfortable bed can make or break a hotel. We stayed in a suite, and our bed was EXTREMELY uncomfortable. To add to the coolness factor, the mattress was placed on a solid wood block with no boxspring. This made for a mattress that progressively felt firmer the longer you slept on it. The worst feeling in the world is to cut your sleep short in the morning because its just too uncomfortable. It took about an hour or so to work the kinks out of our back. In all, this hotel has a laundry list of things going for it. However, only the hotel and room decor is where they appear to have gone the extra mile. Everything else appears to have been added to bolster its amenities list, but not a whole lot of PRACTICAL thought went with it.For me, I wouldn't plan a lengthy vacation at this hotel as the coolness factor will wear out in about 2 days. What you will be left with is a longing for traditional amenities in a more central location.

This isn鈥檛 the typical 鈥渃ontinental鈥?breakfast either 鈥?hard boiled eggs, bagels, toast, juices, french toast, fresh fruit, Starbucks (thank-god) coffee, and other items. There are coin-operated units downstairs for non-suites, but even that is rare for a hotel in my opinion. Okay. Enough already. What are the negatives? Parking (secure, under the hotel) can be a bit tight if you arrive late on a weekend.What can I say? The WT has my loyalty and no other hotel in my 42 years has been able to accomplish that. And we are a PICKY family, believe me. The #1 or #2 or whatever rating was right on baby!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Are You Kidding? #1 in Seattle?? Ok kind readers, its time for a reality check. Location: This hotel is located in the Northern part of Seattle near the U of W. If you have business with the school, or you are visiting your kid in college, this would be a good place to stay. But, if you are a tourist or businessperson, I don鈥檛 think this hotel is for you. I arrived in the evening and I must tell you that my first impression of the neighborhood was that it was kind of scary. The hotel has lots of security and management wants you to know that this place is locked down tight after dark. There are signs throughout the underground parking lot warning you not to leave anything in your car and that the hotel is not responsible for any losses you incur. Oh well, so much for warm, fuzzy-feeling first impressions.Because this property is near the university, the restaurants around the hotel cater to student budgets, so you have lots of nondescript ethnic eateries from which to choose-Thai, Indian, Mexican, Chinese, Pizza, Subway. Typical other businesses you鈥檒l find in the area are barrooms, piercing shops, bodegas, record stores, recycled clothing stores, smoke shops, second-run movie theaters, and hair stylists. Now you get the picture?Rooms: Think dorm room decorated by Ikea. Even though they cleverly added a big mirror to give the illusion of space, I found the rooms to be small and Spartan, but very clean. While the beds are indeed very comfortable, there is no blanket between the sheets and bedspread, so you must use the bedspread to stay warm. Since we all know that hotel bedspreads rarely get washed, I found this to be pretty gross. I鈥檓 not particularly impressed by hotel toiletries because I bring my own stuff when I travel, but you might be charmed by little bottles of Aveda shampoos. There is some kind of gimmicky ala cart menu (not food related) that I have never seen before in a hotel. I really could not be bothered with it, so I cannot offer an opinion, or even tell you what it is.This property offers free breakfast and free internet, both plusses, but overall, there is coldness to this hotel. It has a very pronounced industrial and institutional feel to it. What makes matters worse it that it is not affiliated with any chain, so you don鈥檛 even get travel points.Call me old-fashioned, but whenever I come to Seattle on business, which is quite often, I usually stay downtown. This time, I鈥檝e learned my lesson, I won鈥檛 stray again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Huge rooms at the Watertown I stayed at the Watertown Hotel, located near the university, because I had a special deal from TravelZoo.com for $10 off the regular price. It was a delightful experience and better, for my traveling taste, than the W Hotel downtown (for which I also had a TravelZoo discount). Finding it is easy, parking onsite is easy, and the surrounding neighborhood is interesting and funky. The Watertown has a clever ala cart menu that visitors can use to select carts (literally) for their room based on what theme sounds interesting to them--spa cart comes with bath goodies, art cart comes with crayons and watercolors, baby cart comes with things you'd want if traveling with an infant. You can request a cart in advance or when you check in. My room, located in a corner, was the size of my living and dining rooms at home--I couldn't believe how huge it was. I highly recommend staying at the Watertown and eating at the vegetarian restaurant Carmelita located about 15 minutes' drive away, through a residential area.

<Author>happytrails
<Content>For A Change of Pace..... Watertown advertises itself as a unique urban hotel and it is, offering such amenities as wine tasting in the afternoon, bike rental, and a variety of fun carts that one can reserve free of charge! I chose the spa cart which contained everything I needed to have a relaxing retreat in the bath, right down to music choices (and the best part was no extra charge). The continental breakfast was way above average, the decor very modern and sleek, and not typical of standard hotel room configuration (plus, everything was immaculate). There was a well-stocked little area in the lobby for snack purchases, as well as a nice workout room and conference rooms. The staff was very pleasant and competent, and obviously cared about doing a good job; rates were very reasonable. Contributing to its hip, urban feel was the close proximity of the University of Washington--we enjoyed walking around the area and even found a wonderful little farmer's market several blocks north which offered local specialties in seasonal produce and baked goods. We will definitely make the Watertown our hotel of choice during our next opportunity to visit Seattle!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Style and Location This hotel has a wonderful sense of style about it, and is located in an ideal place for those of you needing to be close to just north of downtown. Our stay at the Watertown was for four nights at the Watertown, in a view room. The room was excellently maintained, and was set up in what I considered to be a very clever configuration. The closet and drawers were part of the walls, and acted as a divider between the bathroom and the rest of the room. Your mileage may vary on that configuration, but the decor and furnishings were very modern art deco-types.One thing to look for are the a la carts, provided by the hotel. These are standalone carts with themes, such as the movie cart, the spa cart, the computer cart, etc. You can request one, and it will be in your room when you arrive. The Spa cart had massagers, foot spas, etc. The computer cart had a computer with printer, which hooked up to the internet. That's all we got, but there was a list of about 15 different ones.The staff we had contact with was very friendly and accomodating, no problems there. There's a morning breakfast spread, including cereal, bagels, boiled eggs, french toast, coffee, orange juice, etc. The dining area for that was very open and comfortable. There is free underground parking underneath the hotel, which was very safe and convenient.This hotel is located in the University district, just north and west of what most people would consider to be the true downtown. It's across the bridge to the north from downtown, but like most of Seattle is still very busy and vibrant. Such as it is, this hotel is ideal if you have business involving the University, but it is literally 3 blocks from I-5, so getting to downtown would take maybe 5 minutes by car.If you're looking to go shopping, there is a cute shopping district to the West, including many well-known stores like Banana Republic. Three blocks to the south across the bridge is Montlake and Capitol Hill. Just across I-5 to the east is the Wallingford district, and to the North and NorthEast is Ravenna and Greenlake. So, some people might quibble about the location, but I really can't see a problem. If you're in Seattle on business and really *need* to be *in* downtown, then you might want something marginally closer. But, if you're in Seattle on leisure, and your focus is the northern area of Seattle (especially the university), I cannot recommend any other hotel.  
<Date>Dec 6, 2004

<Author>kiwibound
<Content>Choose the hotel after reading other reviews We recently returned from a holiday visit to Seattle and we stayed at the Watertown after reading all the positive reviews on this website. As many have already said, this truly is a unique urban hotel. The rooms are clean and modern, with microwave, mini-fridge, coffee maker, and FREE highspeed internet access. We had one of the suites so our room had a fairly large sitting area as well. Complimentary continental breakfast is included (which was fairly good - bagels, muffins, toast, cereals, etc), in the afternoon the front desk has a basket filled with fresh baked cookies, and the evenings offer complimentary wine tasting and you can order appetizers or a light meal (cost for the food). We had a light dinner at the hotel one evening and it was quite tasty! The ala cart program is great - and free! We tried out the spa cart which included everything you need to relax after a busy day of meetings, sightseeing, or shopping.....plus you can either keep your cart for your entire stay, or exchange your cart the next day and give a different theme a try. As mentioned there is no room service or restaurant on site (only the bistro area for breakfast  the evening wine tasting), however there are many restaurants within a few blocks walking distance. One of the best meals we enjoyed was at Mama Melina's - recommended in previous reviews of this hotel and the reason we decided to try it out. It was fantastic - the food, the ambiance, the music, everything about this tiny family run restaurant was enjoyable. It is casual and it is busy, if you go on a weekend you may want to make reservations. If you stay at the Watertown I'd highly recommend a meal (or two!) at Mama Melina's....even if you stay elsewhere in Seattle I'd recommend an enjoyable evening here.Our only complaint about the Watertown was the beds  the noise level on the streets outside. The beds are a mattress on a modern wooden frame - no box spring. They look sleek  match the modern room decor but we found it uncomfortable. The location of our room was on the NW corner of the hotel and the street noise (traffic, university students out on a Friday night, etc) was often loud enough to wake us during the night. Perhaps a different location in the hotel would be better, although I think you'd need to be right in the SE corner. Now if you are a sound sleeper...you probably won't find this to be a problem. For us it was an issue and we ended up shortening our stay at the hotel and eventually moving to another downtown property. Please note we were at the Watertown over a weekend  it also happened to be Halloween weekend so there were LOTS of students out  about partying. The situation may be entirely different during the week.Overall the Watertown truly lives up to its claim as a unique urban hotel with friendly staff and excellent value. I would recommend it to others and simply caution them about our noise trouble (which of course the hotel has no control over). Also...if you check out the Seattle Visitors Bureau website they have a coupon you can print for discounted rates at the Watertown (www.seeseattle.org)  
<Date>Nov 12, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Hotel Recently stayed 3 nights at the Watertown. We received a travel notice from Travelzoo got a rate of $99 per night. Nice new hotel very friendly staff. Good size rooms with a large bathroom area refr/microwave in the room (but can hear traffic noisy and the people next door). The breakfast in the morning is good and they have wine tasting during the week. Good location for the University of Washington area. It's a little far to the downtown area to walk but if you don't have a car the hotel has a free shuttle (very nice driver). The parking in the downtown area is terrible so be prepared to either pay a lot to park at a garage or try to find a meter place on the street. Take note most of the restaurants in the Market Area close at 6 to 6:30 so finding a local place to eat at is kind of hard. If the weather permits suggest going to the Bank of America building on 5th street they have an observation floor that costs just $5 and it's a great view much better than the Space Needle. Try Ivar's Salmon House, and Mama Melina's. Don't forget your umbrella, a sweater and a coat with a hood oh and good walking shoes. It rains a lot in Seattle and it's definitely fall there temp in the 50's to 60's. Try to take a ferry ride to either Bremerton or Bainbridge Island you can drive your car or walk on. We came back from Bremerton at night and the view of downtown Seattle was awesome!!!

<Author>ms_travelwhiz
<Content>A real treasure! I stayed at this lovely, modern, friendly place for business and pleasure and will absolutely be back. From the zen-like calm of the modern lobby (and lapping water over black river stones outside) to the spacious, clean and artfully decorated rooms, this place is a find. Breakfast is included in the room rate and was served in a separate lobby dining area, surrounded by windows and more tasteful furnishings. Week nights brought complementary wine tastings of exciting wines - a great follow up to biking around the area on complementary bikes (with helmets!). Even though it is not in the downtown area, there is an hourly shuttle to drop you and pick you up for business or shopping. Kayaking is just down the hill and there are wonderful restaurants in the area that the very knowledgeable and friendly staff will tell you all about.To top it off, there are the most decadent homemade chocolate chip cookies available at the front desk. But, if you should get hungry, you can pop premium popcorn right in your room in your microwave.This place is a keeper and where I will stay when I am in Seattle.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A few bumps ... We stayed at this property twice within a two week stay. The first time was for three days and the second time was for a single night. There was a mix-up with our first night there and an ADA compliant room that the front desk agents neglected to inform us about. There was no management on duty that night so when I called in the morning and calmly enumerating why I was upset, our problem was swiftly addressed and we were moved into another room for our remaining stay. Despite my initial impression, I gave this property the full stars for several reasons - free high speed Internet, free underground secured parking, free shuttle into town, free Continental breakfast (do not listen to the negative reviews about the food - cold cereals, juice, breads, loads of fresh fruit and yoghurt were just fine to start the day), and lastly free chocolate chip cookies in the afternoons! The management also made me change my mind about my initial review of the Watertown because they listened to my problem and apologized (something that neither of the desk agents on duty did). If you want room service and white glove amenities, go someplace else but if you are looking for a clean, stylish place to rest while exploring Seattle - definitely come here! Besides, you are within walking distance of many university hang-outs and there is a food delivery service that comes to the hotel from a variety of different restaurants. We tried a great pizza place called Pagliacci one night and thoroughly enjoyed it.

<Author>jsb23nc
<Content>GREAT, new hotel with luxury and service Agree with nearly all the previous reviewers. We stayed four days in early August. The Watertown was a wonderful experience. The hotel (lobby and rooms) benefits from its luxurious, contemporary decor. The rooms were reasonably spacious and very clean. Of course, the newness of the hotel helps with the cleanliness and aesthetic value.Our first room had a great view of Mt. Rainier while our second room had an excellent view of downtown Seattle with Rainier still in site! The staff was quite courteous and helpful with directions, restaurant recommendations (Ivar's Salmon House is a must and Mama Melina's was good), et al. Hotel management even allowed us to keep our car parked there for 2 days while we went on 3-day package to Vancouver and Victoria.The add-on carts were a bonus as we used the surf cart to keep abreast of email and stuff going on back at home. The Aveda bath products were another plus. The continental breakfast was much better than those typical of that description. Fresh fruit (bananas, strawberries, and kiwi) was plentiful and the scones were delicious.The only negative one could contemplate would be the distance to downtown Seattle but the complimentary shuttle service got us where we needed to go every day (though, make sure you reserve the shuttle the night before). When we traveled outside of the shuttle times (7:00AM to 7:30PM), the Seattle bus system took us elsewhere (note: these buses stop directly in front of the hotel, are clean, and safe).One final suggestion is to check the Seattle Visitors website and Hotels for reduced rates.An excellent choice for Seattle!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very cool hotel My family and I stayed here for two nights in August 2004 and it was excellent. The rooms were new, very high standard and comfortable, the free carts were great (computer and internet for kids, spa for me) and there was lots of space, big windows and a (distant) view of downtown and mountains. Free parking, good free breakfast, and wine tasting on week day evenings. The staff were extremely friendly and helpful, the best we came across on our trip. Although a little way from Downtown, the hotel runs a shuttle, or there is a bus from right outside which is quick and cheap. Also, a couple of decent places to eat nearby - Mama Melina in particular. Best prices through the website or by calling direct, also check for vouchers on the Seattle Chamber of Commerce website.
